### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 1 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A company that makes wildlife videos purchases camera equipment for $\$ 32,400$. The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years, after which it is considered to have no monetary value. How much is the camera equipment worth 4 years after it is purchased?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 10,800$
  B: $\$ 16,200$
  C: $\$ 21,600$
  D: $\$ 29,700$
Response 0:
Thought:
The equipment depreciates in value at a constant rate for 12 years, which means that its value decreases equally every year. 
The depreciation for each year is calculated as: 
$depreciation = \frac{initial\space value}{useful\space life}$

The initial value of the equipment is $\$ 32,400$. 
The equipment will be used for 12 years. 
Therefore, the depreciation for each year is:
$depreciation = \frac{32400}{12} = \$2700$

The value of the equipment after 4 years can be calculated as:
$final\space value = initial\space value - accumulated\space depreciation$
$final\space value = 32400 - (2700*4)$
$final\space value = \$21,600$

Therefore, the answer is C: $\$21,600$.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The equipment depreciates at a constant rate for 12 years.
  After 12 years, the equipment is considered to have no monetary value.
  Therefore, the equipment depreciates $\$ 32,400/12 = \$ 2,700$ per year.
  4 years after the equipment is purchased, the equipment has depreciated by $\$ 2,700 \times 4 = \$ 10,800$.
  The value of the camera equipment 4 years after it is purchased is $\$ 32,400 - \$ 10,800 = \$ 21,600$.
  Therefore, the answer is C: $\$ 21,600$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:

  Therefore, the yearly depreciation rate is $\frac{\$ 32,400}{12}= \$ 2,700$.
  After 4 years, the equipment will depreciate by $4 \times 2700=\$ 10,800$.
  Therefore, the value of the camera equipment after 4 years is $32,400-10,800=\$ 21,600$.

  Let V be the value of the equipment after 4 years.
  Then, $V = 32,400(1-r)^4$.
  Substituting r = 0.0948, we get V = $21,600$.
  Therefore, the camera equipment is worth $\$ 21,600$ 4 years after it is purchased.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 2 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\frac{a-b}{a}=c$$In the equation above, if $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, which of the following must be true?
Choices:
  A: $c>1$
  B: $c=1$
  C: $c=-1$
  D: $c<-1$
Response 0:
Given: $$\frac{a-b}{a}=c$$where $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive.

We can manipulate the above equation as follows:
\begin{align*}
\frac{a-b}{a}&=c \\
\frac{a}{a} - \frac{b}{a} &= c \\
1 - \frac{b}{a} &= c \\
\frac{b}{a} &= 1-c \\
\end{align*}

Since $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, $\frac{b}{a}$ will be negative. Therefore, $1-c$ must also be negative. This is only possible if $c>1$.

Hence, the answer is A: $c>1$. 

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
We can start by simplifying the equation:
$$\frac{a-b}{a}=c$$
$$1-\frac{b}{a}=c$$
$$\frac{b}{a}=1-c$$

If $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, then $\frac{b}{a}$ is negative. Therefore, $1-c$ must be negative.

If we add $c$ to both sides of the inequality, we get:

$$1 < c$$

So, $c$ must be greater than 1.
Therefore, the answer is A: $c>1$.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought:
  If $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive then $\frac{a-b}{a}$ will be less than 0.
  We can rewrite the equation as $1-\frac{b}{a}=c$.
  Since $b$ is positive and $a$ is negative, the value of $\frac{b}{a}$ is negative and so $1-\frac{b}{a}$ is greater than 1 in absolute value. This implies that c must be less than -1.
  Therefore, the answer is D: $c<-1$.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 3:
Given: $$\frac{a-b}{a}=c$$
$a$ is negative and $b$ is positive.
We can rewrite the equation as $$1-\frac{b}{a}=c.$$Since $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, the fraction $\frac{b}{a}$ is negative.
Therefore, $$1-\frac{b}{a}<1.$$So, $c<1$.
Also, $-1<\frac{b}{a}<0$, so $$-1<c.$$Therefore, the only true statement is $c<1$ which is equivalent to the answer A: $c>1$ being incorrect.

  Therefore, the only possible choice is C: $c=-1$.

Thought:
To solve the equation, we can cross multiply to get:
$$a-b = ac$$
Then, we can factor out $a$ from the right side:
$$a(1-c)=b$$
Given that $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, we know that $(a-b)$ is negative. 
If $(1-c)$ is also negative, then $a(1-c)$ will be positive, contradicting $(a-b)<0$. Therefore, $(1-c)$ must be positive. 
So, $c<1$. 
Now, we need to determine what is the sign of $1-c$ when $c<1$:
$$1-c>0$$
$$\Rightarrow 1> c$$
Thus, we can conclude that the answer is A: $c>1$.

Question: $$h(x)=2^{x}$$The function $h$ is defined above. What is $h(5)-h(3) ?$
Choices:
  A: 2
  B: 4
  C: 24
  D: 28
Response 0:
Thought:  
  $h(x) = 2^x$, so $h(5) = 2^5 = 32$ and $h(3) = 2^3 = 8$
  Therefore, $h(5) - h(3) = 32 - 8 = 24$
  The answer is C: 24
Action: Answer("C")

  Therefore, $h(5)-h(3) = \boxed{\textbf{(C) }24}$

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 4 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If $f(x)=\frac{x^{2}-6 x+3}{x-1}$, what is $f(-1)$ ?
Choices:
  A: -5
  B: -2
  C: 2
  D: 5
Response 0:
Thought: 
  To find $f(-1)$, we can substitute $x=-1$ into the equation $f(x)=\frac{x^{2}-6 x+3}{x-1}$.
  $$
  \begin{aligned} f(-1)&=\frac{(-1)^{2}-6(-1)+3}{-1-1} \\ &=\frac{1+6+3}{-2} \\ &=-\frac{10}{2} \\ &=-5 \end{aligned}
  $$
  Therefore, the answer is A: -5.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
We can directly substitute $x=-1$ in the given function as:
$f(-1) = \frac{(-1)^2 -6(-1)+3}{-1-1} = \frac{1+6+3}{-2} = -5$
Therefore, the answer is A: -5.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 5 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A cylindrical can containing pieces of fruit is filled to the top with syrup before being sealed. The base of the can has an area of $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$, and the height of the can is $10 \mathrm{~cm}$. If $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$ of syrup is needed to fill the can to the top, which of the following is closest to the total volume of the pieces of fruit in the can?
Choices:
  A: $7.5 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  B: $185 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  C: $640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
  D: $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The volume of the cylindrical can is $V_{can}=Bh$, where $B$ is the area of its base and $h$ is its height.
  We are given that $B=75\mathrm{~cm}^{2}$ and $h=10\mathrm{~cm}$.
  Therefore, $V_{can}=Bh=75\mathrm{~cm}^{2}\cdot 10\mathrm{~cm}=750\mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The volume of the syrup is $110\mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The total volume of the can when it is filled with syrup and fruit pieces is $750\mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  Therefore, the volume of the fruit pieces is the difference between the total volume of the can and the volume of the syrup.
  So, the volume of the fruit pieces is $V_{pieces}=750\mathrm{~cm}^{3}-110\mathrm{~cm}^{3}=640\mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  The answer is C: $640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The volume of the cylindrical can is calculated using the formula V = πr^2h, where r is the radius of the base and h is the height of the can.
  We know that the area of the base of the cylindrical can is 75 cm^2. 
  The formula for the area of a circle is A = πr^2.
  Solving for r, we get r = √(75/π) cm.
  The volume of the cylindrical can is given as 110 cm^3.
  We can solve for the volume of the pieces of fruit by subtracting the volume of the syrup from the volume of the can.
  The answer is D: 750 cm^3.
  
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  The volume of a cylinder is given by the formula $V=\pi r^{2}h$.
  The area of the base of the cylinder is $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$, so the radius is $\sqrt{75/(\pi)} \approx 4.14 \mathrm{~cm}$.
  The height of the cylinder is 10 cm.
  The volume of syrup required to fill the can is $110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$, so the total volume of the can is  $V=\pi r^{2}h \approx (3.14)\cdot (4.14)^{2} \cdot 10 \approx 541 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  Therefore, the volume of the fruit in the can is $541 - 110 = 431 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.
  Among the choices given, the closest number to $431$ is $750$.

  We know that the area of the base is $75 \mathrm{~cm}^{2}$ and the height of the can is $10 \mathrm{~cm}$.

  Therefore, the volume of the fruits is $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} - 110 \mathrm{~cm}^{3} = 640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$. 
  The answer is C: $640 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.

  We can do this by using the formula V = Ah for the cylinder and then subtracting the volume of the syrup.
  We get V = (75 $\mathrm{cm}^{2}$)($10 \mathrm{~cm}$) - 110 $\mathrm{cm}^{3}$ = 440 $\mathrm{cm}^{3}$.
  Therefore, the total volume of the fruit pieces is 440 $\mathrm{cm}^{3}$.
  The answer is D: $750 \mathrm{~cm}^{3}$.

Question: If $y=k x$, where $k$ is a constant, and $y=24$ when $x=6$, what is the value of $y$ when $x=5$ ?
Choices:
  A: 6
  B: 15
  C: 20
  D: 23
Response 0:
Thought:
  Since $y=kx$, we can use the information when $x=6$ to solve for $k$.
  If $y=24$ and $x=6$, then $24=k*6$, so $k=24/6=4$.
  Now we can use $k=4$ and $x=5$ to solve for $y$.
  If $y=kx$ and $k=4$ and $x=5$, then $y=4*5=20$.
  Therefore, when $x=5$, $y$ is equal to 20.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  If $y=k x$, then $k$ is the slope of the line that represents the relationship between $x$ and $y$.
  We can use the point-slope form $y-y_1=k(x-x_1)$ of a line to determine $k$.
  Since $y=24$ when $x=6$, we have $24=k(6)$, which gives $k=4$.
  Now we can use $k$ to find $y$ when $x=5$ by substituting $k$ and $x$ in the equation $y=k x$.
  We get $y=4(5)=20$.
  Therefore, the answer is C: 20.

Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{array}{r}3 x+4 y=-23 \\2 y-x=-19\end{array}$$What is the solution $(x, y)$ to the system of equations above?
Choices:
  A: $(-5,-2)$
  B: $(3,-8)$
  C: $(4,-6)$
  D: $(9,-6)$
Response 0:
Thought:
  One way to solve this system is to use substitution method.
  Solve the second equation for $x$:  $$x = 2y+19$$
  Substitute $x = 2y+19$ into the first equation and solve for $y$: $$3(2y+19)+4y=-23$$
  $$6y+57+4y=-23$$
  $$10y = -80$$
  $$y=-8$$
  Substitute $y=-8$ back into the second equation to solve for $x$: $$x = 2y+19 = 2(-8)+19 = 3$$
  The solution of the system is $(x, y) = (3,-8)$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:

  Simplify and solve for y: $10y = -80 \implies y = -8$
  Substitute $y = -8$ back into the second equation to solve for $x$: $x = 2(-8) + 19 = 3$
  Thus, the solution to the system of equations is $(x, y) = (3, -8)$

Dividing both sides by $1.08$, we have $t=\frac{a-1,052}{1.08}$.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 10 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If $2 w+4 t=14$ and $4 w+5 t=25$, what is the value of $2 w+3 t ?$
Choices:
  A: 6
  B: 10
  C: 13
  D: 17
Response 0:
Thought:
  We are given two equations
  $$
  \begin{aligned}
  2 w+4 t&=14\\
  4 w+5 t&=25\\
  \end{aligned}
  $$
  If we multiply the first equation by $2$ and subtract the second equation from it, we can eliminate $w$ and solve for $t$.
  $$
  \begin{aligned}
  4 w+8 t &= 28\\
  4 w+5 t &= 25\\
  \hline\\
  3 t &= 3\\
  t &= 1\\
  \end{aligned}
  $$
  Now that we know the value of $t$, we can substitute it into the first equation to solve for $w$.
  $$
  \begin{aligned}
  2 w+4(1)&=14\\
  2 w&=10\\
  w&=5\\
  \end{aligned}
  $$
  Finally, we can plug in $w=5$ and $t=1$ into the expression $2w+3t$ to get the answer.
  $$
  2w+3t = 2(5)+3(1)=13
  $$
  Therefore, the answer is C: 13.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We need to find a way to eliminate one of the variables for us to solve for the other variable.
  Multiplying the first equation by 2 produces $4w+8t=28$, which can be subtracted from the second equation $4w+5t=25$ to give $t=-3$.
  Substituting t=-3 in either of the two original equations can solve for w.
  $2w+4(-3)=14$ simplifies to $2w=26$, which gives us $w=13$.
  $2w+3t$ can now be computed as $2(13)+3(-3)=20$.
  Therefore, the value of $2w+3t$ is 20.
Action: Answer("None of the above")

    \begin{aligned}
    2 w+4 t &=14 \\
    4 w+5 t &=25
     \end{aligned}

    \begin{aligned}
    &\begin{aligned}
    &(2w+4t)\times -2\\
    &\hspace{7mm}-\\
    &(4w+5t)\\
    \end{aligned} \\
    &-6t = -18 \\
    &\Rightarrow t = 3 \\

    \end{cases}\\

    \begin{cases}

    t &= 3
    \end{cases}
    \end{aligned}

  Therefore, the answer is 7.

Response 3:
Thought:
We want to find the value of  $2 w+3 t$ 
Multiplying the first equation by $2$ gives $4 w+8 t=28$
Multiplying the second equation by $-3$ gives $-12 w-15 t=-75$
Adding the above equations leaves us with $-8t = -47$
Solving for $t$, we get $t = \frac{47}{8}$

Question: If $x>3$, which of the following is equivalent to $\frac{1}{\frac{1}{x+2}+\frac{1}{x+3}}$ ?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{2 x+5}{x^{2}+5 x+6}$
  B: $\frac{x^{2}+5 x+6}{2 x+5}$
  C: $2 x+5$
  D: $x^{2}+5 x+6$
Response 0:
Thought:
  First, we need to simplify the expression in the parentheses.
  The common denominator is $(x+2)(x+3)$.
  Therefore, $\frac{1}{\frac{1}{x+2}+\frac{1}{x+3}} = \frac{(x+2)(x+3)}{(x+3)+(x+2)}$.
  Simplifying further, $\frac{(x+2)(x+3)}{2x+5} = \frac{(x+2)(x+3)}{1(2x+5)}$.
  The numerator can be factored as $x^2 + 5x+6$.
  Therefore, the correct answer is B: $\frac{x^{2}+5 x+6}{2 x+5}$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  To find the equivalent expression, we need to simplify the given expression.
  Let's start by finding the common denominator of the two fractions in the denominator of the given expression.
  The common denominator is $(x+2)(x+3)$.
  So, we can write $\frac{1}{\frac{(x+2)+(x+3)}{(x+2)(x+3)}}$.
  Simplifying this gives $\frac{1}{\frac{2x+5}{(x+2)(x+3)}}$.
  We can then multiply the numerator and denominator of the fraction in the denominator by $(x+2)(x+3)$ to get a single fraction in the denominator.
  This gives us $\frac{1}{\frac{2x+5}{x^{2}+5x+6}}$.
  We can then flip the fraction in the denominator and multiply it with the fraction in the numerator to get the equivalent expression.
  So, the final expression is $\frac{x^{2}+5x+6}{2x+5}$.
  Therefore, the answer is B: $\frac{x^{2}+5x+6}{2x+5}$.

  $x^2+5x+6$

Question: $$(a x+3)\left(5 x^{2}-b x+4\right)=20 x^{3}-9 x^{2}-2 x+12$$The equation above is true for all $x$, where $a$ and $b$ are constants. What is the value of $a b$ ?
Choices:
  A: 18
  B: 20
  C: 24
  D: 40
Response 0:
Thought:
  We should start with simplifying the equation by multiplying out the left-hand side.
  $(a x+3)\left(5 x^{2}-b x+4\right)=20 x^{3}-9 x^{2}-2 x+12$ can be written as $5ax^3- abx^2+20ax^2-3bx^2+15x+12ax-12b=20 x^{3}-9 x^{2}-2 x+12$
  Summing the like terms $5ax^3+20ax^2+12ax-3bx^2- abx^2-12b=20 x^{3}-9 x^{2}-2 x+12$
  Equating the coefficients of like terms, we get $5a=20$, $20a-3b=0$, and $12a- ab=-2$.
  So, $a=4$ from the first equation.
  Substituting $a$ value in second equation, $20(4)-3b=0$, so $b=\frac{80}{3}$.
  Substituting $a$ and $b$ values in third equation, $12(4)-\frac{80}{3}(4)=\frac{-16}{3}$.
  Therefore, $ab=\frac{80}{3}*4=80/3*4=320/3$.

  $$5a x^{3}−ab x^{2}+20ax^{2}+12x^{2}-3bx+15x+12=20 x^{3}-9 x^{2}-2 x+12$$
  Then, grouping like terms we get:
  $$5a x^{3}+(20a-12)x^{2}+(-ab+15)x+12=20 x^{3}-9 x^{2}-2 x+12$$
  By equating the coefficients of the like terms on both sides, we get:
  $$\begin{cases} 5a=20\\ 20a-12=-9\\ -ab+15=-2 \end{cases}$$

  $$5ax^3 -abx^2 + 20ax^2 -3bx + 15x^2 + 12ax + 12 = 20x^3 - 9x^2 -2x + 12$$

  $$5ax^3 + (20a - ab + 15)x^2 + (12a - 3b)x + 12 = 20x^3 - 9x^2 - 2x + 12$$

  \begin{align*}
    20a - ab +15 &= 0 \quad ...(1) \\
    12a - 3b &= -2 \quad ...(2)
  \end{align*}

    &= 4a^2 - \frac{2a}{3} \\
    &= 4\left(\frac{5 + \frac{11\sqrt{3}}{3}}{2}\right)^2 - \frac{2}{3}\left(\frac{5 + \frac{11\sqrt{3}}{3}}{2}\right) \\
    &\approx \boxed{\textbf{(A) } 18}
  \end{align*}

  Multiplying $(a x+3)\left(5 x^{2}-b x+4\right)$ gives $20 x^{3}-9 x^{2}-2 x+12$.
  We want to find the value of $ab$.
  Let's first expand the left side of the equation and see if it leads us to a solution.
  $$(a x+3)(5 x^{2}-b x+4) = 5ax^3 - abx^2 + (20 - 3ab)x + 12$$
  Comparing this to $20 x^{3}-9 x^{2}-2 x+12$, we see that $5a = 20$, $20 - 3ab = 0$, and $ab$ is what we are solving for.
  Solving for $a$ gives $a = 4$.
  Substituting $a = 4$ into the second equation $20 - 3ab = 0$, we get $20 - 3 \times 4 \times b = 0$.
  Solving for $b$, we get $b = \frac{5}{6}$.
  Therefore, $ab = 4 \times \frac{5}{6} = \frac{10}{3}$.

  Imaginary parts: $3i+9i=12i$.

  The answer is A: $-1+12 i$.

  Therefore, the sum $(7+3 i)+(-8+9 i)$ is equal to $-1+12 i$.

Question: If $a^{2}+b^{2}=z$ and $a b=y$, which of the following is equivalent to $4 z+8 y$ ?
Choices:
  A: $(a+2 b)^{2}$
  B: $(2 a+2 b)^{2}$
  C: $(4 a+4 b)^{2}$
  D: $(4 a+8 b)^{2}$
Response 0:
Thought:
We can substitute $z = a^{2}+b^{2}$ and $y = a b$ into $4z + 8y$.
Thus, we get:
$4z + 8y = 4(a^{2}+b^{2})+ 8(ab)$
$= 4a^{2}+4b^{2}+8ab$
$= 4(a^{2}+2ab+b^{2})$
$= 4(a+b)^{2}$
Therefore, the answer is A: $(a+2b)^{2}$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Given $a^{2}+b^{2}=z$, we know that $(a+b)^2 = a^2+2ab+b^2 = z+2y$.
  Therefore, $4z+8y = 4(a^2+b^2) + 8ab = 4(a+b)^2 = (2a+2b)^2$
  The answer is B: $(2 a+2 b)^{2}$
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:
Using algebraic manipulation, we can rewrite $4z+8y$ in terms of $a$ and $b$.
$4z+8y=4(a^2+b^2)+8(ab)$
$4z+8y=4a^2+4b^2+8ab$
$4z+8y=(2a)^2+2\times2a\times2b+(2b)^2$
$4z+8y=(2a+2b)^2$
Therefore, the answer is B: $(2a+2b)^2$.

$(a+b)^2 + 2ab= a^2+b^2+2ab+2ab$
$(a+b)^2 + 2ab= a^2+2ab+b^2$
$(a+b)^2 = a^2+2ab+b^2$ − $2ab$
$(a+b)^2 = (a^2+b^2+2ab)$
$(a+b)^2 = z+2y$
We can rewrite $4z+8y$ as $4(a^2+b^2)+8(ab)$ as $4(a^2+b^2+2ab)$ which is equal to $4(z+2y)$.

A: $(a+2b)^2 = a^2+4ab+4b^2$ which is not equivalent to $4z+8y$.

B: $(2a+2b)^2 = 4a^2+8ab+4b^2$ which is equivalent to $4z+8y$.

C: $(4a+4b)^2 = 16a^2+32ab+16b^2$ which is not equivalent to $4z+8y$.

D: $(4a+8b)^2 = 16a^2+64ab+64b^2$ which is not equivalent to $4z+8y$.

Therefore the answer is B: $(2a+2b)^2$.

Topic: Math
Question: Shipping Charges\begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|}\hline$\begin{array}{c}\text { Merchandise weight } \\ \text { (pounds) }\end{array}$ & $\begin{array}{c}\text { Shipping } \\ \text { charge }\end{array}$ \\\hline5 & $\$ 16.94$ \\\hline10 & $\$ 21.89$ \\\hline20 & $\$ 31.79$ \\\hline40 & $\$ 51.59$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}The table above shows shipping charges for an online retailer that sells sporting goods. There is a linear relationship between the shipping charge and the weight of the merchandise. Which function can be used to determine the total shipping charge $f(x)$, in dollars, for an order with a merchandise weight of $x$ pounds?
Choices:
  A: $f(x)=0.99 x$
  B: $f(x)=0.99 x+11.99$
  C: $f(x)=3.39 x$
  D: $f(x)=3.39 x+16.94$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We are given that there is a linear relationship between the shipping charge and the weight of the merchandise.
  A linear relation between two variables can be modeled using a linear equation of the form $y = mx + b$.
  In the equation, $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  We can find the slope of the line passing through two points using the formula $m = \frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1}$.
  Using the points $(5, 16.94)$ and $(40, 51.59)$ we can compute the slope of the line.
  Once we have determined the slope of the line, we can use the y-intercept to write the equation of the line in the slope-intercept form $y = mx + b$.
  
Action: 
  Using the formula for slope we have, $m = \frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1} = \frac{51.59-16.94}{40-5} = 1.15$.
  Using the slope and the point $(5, 16.94)$, we can use the slope-intercept form to find the value of $b$. We have $y = mx + b$, or $16.94 = 1.15(5) + b$. Therefore, $b = 10.39$.
  Thus, the equation for the shipping cost based on merchandise weight is $f(x) = 1.15x + 10.39$.
  The answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(B)}\ f(x)=0.99x+11.99}$.
Response 1:
Thought: Since there is a linear relationship between the shipping charge and the weight of the merchandise, we can use the slope-intercept form to determine the function that represents the data.
- The slope ($m$) is the change in the shipping charge divided by the change in the weight of the merchandise.  So, we can pick any two points from the table and calculate the slope. Let's use the points $(5,16.94)$ and $(40,51.59)$.
  $$m = \dfrac{51.59 - 16.94}{40 - 5} \approx 0.99$$
- The $y$-intercept is the shipping charge when the weight of the merchandise is zero. Since this situation doesn't make sense in this context, the $y$-intercept is the initial cost that the customer has to pay before the weight of the merchandise is taken into account. In this case, it seems that the initial cost is $\$ 16.94 - 5(\$ 0.99) = \$ 11.99$. 
- Therefore, the equation of the function is $f(x) = 0.99x + 11.99$.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 17 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Context: $$.\begin{aligned}.& \text { Mosteller's formula: } A=\frac{\sqrt{h w}}{60} \\.& \text { Current's formula: } A=\frac{4+w}{30}.\end{aligned}.$$.The formulas above are used in medicine to estimate the body surface area $A$, in square meters, of infants and children whose weight $w$ ranges between 3 and 30 kilograms and whose height $h$ is measured in centimeters.
Question: Based on Current's formula, what is $w$ in terms of $A$ ?
Choices:
  A: $w=30 A-4$
  B: $w=30 A+4$
  C: $w=30(A-4)$
  D: $w=30(A+4)$

  We can solve for $w$ by using algebraic manipulation.
  Start with $A = \frac{4+w}{30}$.
  Multiply both sides of the equation by 30: $30A = 4 + w$.
  Subtract 4 from both sides of the equation: $w = 30A - 4$.
  Therefore, the answer is A: $w=30A-4$.

Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|c|c|}\hline$x$ & $a$ & $3 a$ & $5 a$ \\\hline$y$ & 0 & $-a$ & $-2 a$ \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}Some values of $x$ and their corresponding values of $y$ are shown in the table above, where $a$ is a constant. If there is a linear relationship between $x$ and $y$, which of the following equations represents the relationship?
Choices:
  A: $x+2 y=a$
  B: $x+2 y=5 a$
  C: $2 x-y=-5 a$
  D: $2 x-y=7 a$
Response 0:
Thought:
We can start by finding the slope of the linear equation, using the values of $x$ and $y$ from two rows of the table. We can choose the top and middle rows for this. Then we can plug in the slope and one of the points into the point-slope form equation for a line and simplify it to one of the answer choices.
  - The changes in $x$ are $3a-a=2a$ and $5a-3a=2a$, respectively.
  - The corresponding changes in $y$ are $-a-0=-a$ and $-2a-(-a)=-a$.
  - The slope of the line is $\frac{\Delta y}{\Delta x}=\frac{-a}{2a}=-\frac{1}{2}$.
  - Choosing the top row as a reference point, we have $x=a$ and $y=0$.
  - Using the point-slope form, we can write $y-0 = -\frac{1}{2}(x-a)$.
  - Simplifying, we get $y=-\frac{1}{2}x+\frac{1}{2}a$.
  - Rearranging this equation, we find $x+2y=a$.
  - Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(A)}\ x+2 y=a}$. 

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  To determine which equation represents the linear relationship between $x$ and $y$, we have to find two data points and calculate the slope between them. Because it is a linear relationship, the slope should be constant, regardless of which two data points we choose.

  When $x = 5a$, $y = -2a$
  When $x = a$, $y = 0$
  The slope between these two points is $\frac{0-(-2a)}{a-5a} = \frac{1}{2}$
  Now, let us substitute this slope into each of the equations, and see which equation satisfies all the data points in the table.
  A: $x+2y=a$ becomes $5a+2(-2a)=a$, which simplifies to $a=a$ (true)
  B: $x+2y=5a$ becomes $5a+2(-2a)=5a$, which simplifies to $a=a$ (true)
  C: $2x-y=-5a$ becomes $2(5a)-(-2a)=-5a$, which simplifies to $a=-5a$ (false)
  D: $2x-y=7a$ becomes $2(5a)-(-2a)=7a$, which simplifies to $12a=7a$ (false)
  Therefore, the correct answer is either A or B.
  To confirm, we need to pick another data point from the table and see if it satisfies the equation we choose.
  Let us choose the second data point $(x=a,y=-a)$.
  When $x=a$, $y=-a$,
  A: $a+2(-a)=a$ which simplifies to $a=a$ (true)
  B: $a+2(-a)=5a$ which simplifies to $3a=5a$ (false)
  Therefore, the equation that represents the linear relationship between $x$ and $y$ is A: $x+2y=a$

Based on the information given in the box above, how many 1-milligram doses are there in one 2-decagram container?
Choices:
  A: $\quad 0.002$
  B: $\quad 200$
  C: $\quad 2,000$
  D: 20,000
Response 0:
Thought:
  1 decagram = 10 grams
  1 gram = 1,000 milligrams
  2-decagram container = 2 × 10 = 20 grams
  Number of 1-milligram doses in 1 gram = 1,000 doses
  Number of 1-milligram doses in 20 grams = 20 x 1,000 doses = 20,000 doses
  Therefore, there are 20,000 1-milligram doses in one 2-decagram container
  The answer is D: 20,000
  
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  1 decagram = 10 grams
  1,000 milligrams = 1 gram
  Thus, 1 milligram = 1/1000 gram
  Therefore, 1 decagram = $10 \times 1000$ milligrams = $10,000$ milligrams
  A 2-decagram container contains 2 x 10,000 = 20,000 milligrams of medicine.
  Therefore, there are 20,000 1-milligram doses in one 2-decagram container.

  1,000 milligrams = 1 gram
  In order to convert decagram to milligrams, we need to convert decagram to grams and then grams to milligrams.
  1 decagram = 10 grams = 10 * 1,000 milligrams = 10,000 milligrams
  So, 2 decagrams = 2 * 10,000 = 20,000 milligrams
  Each 1-milligram dose requires 1/1,000 = 0.001 gram or 0.1 decagrams
  Therefore, there are 20,000 / 0.1 = 200,000 doses of medicine in one 2-decagram container.
  The answer is not among the available choices, however, the closest value to the actual answer is 200 represented by the choice B.

  1,000 milligrams = 1 gram

$$

$$

To convert 20 grams to milligrams:
$$
20 \text{ grams} \cdot \dfrac{1,000 \text{ milligrams}}{1 \text{ gram}} = 20,000 \text{ milligrams}
$$
  
One 2-decagram container has 20,000 milligrams of medicine.

$$
20,000 \text{ milligrams} \cdot \dfrac{1 \text{ dose}}{1 \text{ milligram}} = 20,000 \text{ doses}
$$

Therefore, there are 20,000 1-milligram doses in one 2-decagram container of medicine.

  B: 0
  C: 1

$g(0)=2(0)-1=-1$.
Now substituting $g(0)$ in the equation of $h(x)$.
$h(x)= 1- g(x)=1- (2x-1)=2-2x$
Therefore $h(0)=2$.

Question: A circle in the $x y$-plane has center $(5,7)$ and radius 2. Which of the following is an equation of the circle?
Choices:
  A: $(x-5)^{2}+(y-7)^{2}=4$
  B: $(x+5)^{2}+(y+7)^{2}=4$
  C: $(x-5)^{2}+(y-7)^{2}=2$
  D: $(x+5)^{2}+(y+7)^{2}=2$
Response 0:
Thought: 
The equation of a circle is of the form $(x-h)^2 + (y-k)^2=r^2$ where (h,k) is the center of the circle and r is the radius. 
We are given that the center is (5,7) and the radius is 2. 
Therefore, we should choose the equation that has center (5,7) and radius 2. 
The answer is A: $(x-5)^{2}+(y-7)^{2}=4$.

Question: $$y=-(x-3)^{2}+a$$In the equation above, $a$ is a constant. The graph of the equation in the $x y$-plane is a parabola. Which of the following is true about the parabola?
Choices:
  A: Its minimum occurs at $(-3, a)$.
  B: Its minimum occurs at $(3, a)$.
  C: Its maximum occurs at $(-3, a)$.
  D: Its maximum occurs at $(3, a)$.
Response 0:
Thought:
  The equation given is in vertex form: $$y=a-(x-3)^{2}$$
  The vertex form of the equation of a parabola is given by:
    $$y=a(x-h)^{2}+k$$
  where (h, k) is the vertex of the parabola.
  Comparing this with the given equation, we can see that:
    h = 3 and k = a
  The coefficient in front of the squared term is negative, indicating that the graph is facing downwards.
  Therefore, the vertex is the maximum point on the parabola.
  The vertex is at point $(h, k) = (3, a)$.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Its maximum occurs at $(3, a)$. 
Action: Answer("D")

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 24 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A psychologist set up an experiment to study the tendency of a person to select the first item when presented with a series of items. In the experiment, 300 people were presented with a set of five pictures arranged in random order. Each person was asked to choose the most appealing picture. Of the first 150 participants, 36 chose the first picture in the set. Among the remaining 150 participants, $p$ people chose the first picture in the set. If more than $20 \%$ of all participants chose the first picture in the set, which of the following inequalities best describes the possible values of $p$ ?
Choices:
  A: $p>0.20(300-36)$, where $p \leq 150$
  B: $p>0.20(300+36)$, where $p \leq 150$
  C: $p-36>0.20(300)$, where $p \leq 150$
  D: $p+36>0.20(300)$, where $p \leq 150$
Response 0:
Thought:
  Out of 150 people in the first group, 36 chose the first picture in the set.
  Out of 150 people in the second group, $p$ chose the first picture in the set.
  The number of people who chose the first picture among all participants is $36+p$.
  More than 20% of the 300 participants chose the first picture in the set, so at least 60 people chose the first picture.
  In the worst-case scenario, all 36 people in the first group who chose the first picture among the five pictures chose it just because it was the first, and none of the people in the second group chose it for the same reason.
  In that case, $p$ would be zero, and a total of 36 people would choose the first picture among all participants. But the problem says that more than 20% of the participants chose the first picture, so this case is not possible.
  Therefore, $p$ must be greater than zero.
  Also, the number of people who chose the first picture among all participants must be greater than 20% of the total number of participants, which is 60.
  $36+p$ must be greater than 60.
  The possible values of $p$ are between 0 and 114 (which occurs when all 150 people in the first group chose the first picture, and 60 people in the second group chose it as well).
  Therefore, $p$ satisfies the inequality $0<p \leq 114$.
  Inequality C: $p-36>0.20(300)$, where $p \leq 150$ does not make sense because the left side is always greater than the maximum value on the right side.
  Inequality D: $p+36>0.20(300)$, where $p \leq 150$ does not hold in the worst-case scenario described above, where $p$ equals zero.
  Inequality A: $p>0.20(300-36)$, where $p \leq 150$ holds, but it is too restrictive, as it implies $p\leq 114$ which is not necessarily true.
  Inequality B: $p>0.20(300+36)$, where $p \leq 150$ holds and is also the most accurate description of the possible values of $p$.
  Therefore, the answer is B: $p>0.20(300+36)$, where $p \leq 150$. 
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought: 
Let's start by finding out how many of the first 150 people did NOT choose the first picture in the set. 
  Since there are 5 pictures in the set, the probability that a person does not choose the first picture is $4/5$.
  Therefore, the expected number of people who do not choose the first picture is $4/5 \times 150 = 120$.
  This means that $150-36-120 = 6$ of the first 150 people chose a picture other than the first one.
  Now we need to find the minimum number of people among the remaining 150 who need to choose the first picture in order to satisfy the condition that more than $20 \%$ of all participants chose the first picture.
  The total number of people who chose the first picture is $36+p$. 
  The total number of people is 300. 
  Therefore, we need $36+p > 0.20(300) = 60$ people to choose the first picture.
  This means $p > 24$.
  Since $p$ cannot be greater than 150, we have $24 < p \leq 150$.
  The inequality that best describes this is (D) $p+36>0.20(300)$, where $p \leq 150$.
Action: Answer("D")

The percentage of people who chose the 1st picture is $\frac{36+p}{300}$.
Since we want this percentage to be more than $20 \%$, we have $\frac{36+p}{300}>0.20$.
Multiplying both sides by 300 gives $36+p>0.20(300)=60$.
Solving for $p$ gives $p>60-36=24$.
We are also given that $p\leq 150$.
Therefore, the possible values of $p$ are $24<p\leq 150$.
Among the answer choices, only (A) gives this range.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 25 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Which of the following is an equivalent form of $(1.5 x-2.4)^{2}-\left(5.2 x^{2}-6.4\right) ?$
Choices:
  A: $-2.2 x^{2}+1.6$
  B: $-2.2 x^{2}+11.2$
  C: $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+12.16$
  D: $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+0.64$
Response 0:
Thought:
Use the following binomic formula: $(a+b)^2 = a^2 + 2ab + b^2$ to expand the left-hand side of the expression. 
\begin{align*}
    & (1.5x - 2.4)^2 - (5.2x^2 - 6.4) \\
    =& \ (1.5x)^2 - 2\cdot 1.5x \cdot 2.4 + (2.4)^2 - 5.2x^2 + 6.4\\
    =& \ 2.25x^2 - 7.2x + 5.76 - 5.2x^2 + 6.4\\
    =& \ -2.95x^2 - 7.2x + 12.16
\end{align*}
Therefore, the answer is (C) $-2.95x^2 - 7.2x + 12.16$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
We can start simplifying the equation by expanding the square of $1.5x-2.4$ and distributing the negative sign to the expression on the right.

$(1.5 x-2.4)^{2}-\left(5.2 x^{2}-6.4\right) = (1.5x - 2.4)(1.5x - 2.4) - (5.2x^2 - 6.4)$

$= (2.25x^2 - 3.6x - 3.6x + 5.76) - 5.2x^2 + 6.4$

$= -2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+0.64$

Therefore, the answer is D: $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+0.64$.

Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought:
Use the following steps to expand the given expression:
 - $(1.5x-2.4)^2 - (5.2x^2 - 6.4) = ((1.5x)^2 - 2(1.5x)(2.4) + (2.4)^2) - (5.2x^2 - 6.4)$
 - Simplify the expression using the distributive property, combining like terms, and performing the subtraction of the two expressions.
 - The equivalent form will have the highest exponent of $x$ to be $x^2$.
Let's apply these steps to each answer choice:
  A) $-2.2 x^{2}+1.6$:
    - $(1.5x-2.4)^2 - (5.2x^2 - 6.4) = 2.25x^2 - 7.2x + 5.76 - 5.2x^2 + 6.4 = -2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+12.16$
    - NOT equivalent to the original expression
  B) $-2.2 x^{2}+11.2$:
    - $(1.5x-2.4)^2 - (5.2x^2 - 6.4) = 2.25x^2 - 7.2x + 5.76 - 5.2x^2 + 6.4 = -2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+12.16$
    - NOT equivalent to the original expression
  C) $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+12.16$:
    - $(1.5x-2.4)^2 - (5.2x^2 - 6.4) = 2.25x^2 - 7.2x + 5.76 - 5.2x^2 + 6.4 = -2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+12.16$
    - Equivalent to the original expression
  D) $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+0.64$:
    - $(1.5x-2.4)^2 - (5.2x^2 - 6.4) = 2.25x^2 - 7.2x + 5.76 - 5.2x^2 + 6.4 = -2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+12.16$
    - NOT equivalent to the original expression
Therefore, the equivalent form of $(1.5 x-2.4)^{2}-\left(5.2 x^{2}-6.4\right)$ is $-2.95 x^{2}-7.2 x+12.16$, which is choice C.

Response 3:
Thought:
  Start by expanding $(1.5 x-2.4)^{2}$:
  $(1.5 x-2.4)^{2} = (1.5 x)^2 - 2\cdot 1.5 x \cdot 2.4 + (2.4)^2 = 2.25 x^2 - 7.2 x + 5.76$
  Distribute the negative sign on the expression $\left(5.2 x^{2}-6.4\right)$: $-\left(5.2 x^{2}-6.4\right)= -5.2 x^{2}+6.4$

Question: In the $x y$-plane, the line determined by the points $(2, k)$ and $(k, 32)$ passes through the origin. Which of the following could be the value of $k$ ?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 4
  C: 8
  D: 16
Response 0:
Thought:
  If the line passes through the origin, then the line must have an equation of the form $y=mx$.
  We know that the line passes through the points $(2, k)$ and $(k, 32)$.
  Therefore, the slope of the line is given by $m=\frac{32-k}{k-2}$.
  If the line passes through the origin, then we must have $k m = k \cdot \frac{32-k}{k-2} = 32$.
  We can simplify this equation to get $k^2 - 34k + 64 = 0$.
  We can solve this quadratic equation to get $k=2$ or $k=32$.
  We are looking for a value of $k$ that appears in the answer choices; this is $\boxed{\textbf{(C) } 8}$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We can use the fact that the line passes through the origin to find k.
  The equation of the line can be found using the slope-intercept form:
  $y = mx + b$
  $m = \frac{y_2 - y_1}{x_2 - x_1}$
  $k = y_1 = mx_1 + b$
  $32 = mk + b$
  In this case, the y-intercept is 0 since the line passes through the origin. Therefore, $b = 0$.
  Substituting into the second equation gives $32 = mk$.
  
Analysis:
  A: If $k=0$, then $mk = 0$, which satisfies the condition. This choice is possible.
  B: If $k=4$, then $mk = 128$, which is not 32. This choice is not possible.
  C: If $k=8$, then $mk = 256$, which is not 32. This choice is not possible.
  D: If $k=16$, then $mk = 512$, which is not 32. This choice is not possible.

Thought: 
To solve the problem, we need to find the equation of the line determined by $(2, k)$ and $(k, 32)$. 

First, we need to find the slope of the line. We know that the line passes through the origin, so it must pass through the point $(0, 0)$. The slope of the line passing through these two points is:

$$\begin{aligned} m &= \dfrac{32-k}{k-2} \\ &= -\dfrac{32-k}{2-k} \\ &= \dfrac{k-32}{k-2} \end{aligned}$$

Next, we can use the point-slope form of a line to find the equation of the line. We know that the line passes through the point $(2, k)$, so the equation of the line is:

$$y - k = m(x - 2)$$

Since the line passes through the origin, we know that $(0, 0)$ is also a point on the line. We can substitute these values into the equation to get:

$$\begin{aligned}0 - k &= m(0 - 2) \\ -k &= -2m \\ k &= 2m\end{aligned}$$

Now, we can substitute our expression for $m$ into this equation:

$$\begin{aligned} k &= 2 \left( \dfrac{k-32}{k-2} \right) \\ k(k-2) &= 2(k-32) \\ k^2-2k &= 2k-64 \\ k^2-4k+64 &= 0\end{aligned}$$

We can solve for $k$ by factoring the quadratic:

$$k^2-4k+64 = (k-2)^2 + 60 = 0$$

The only possible value of $k$ is therefore $\boldsymbol{D: 16}$.

Question: If 50 one-cent coins were stacked on top of each other in a column, the column would be approximately $3 \frac{7}{8}$ inches tall. At this rate, which of the following is closest to the number of one-cent coins it would take to make an 8-inch-tall column?
Choices:
  A: 75
  B: 100
  C: 200
  D: 390
Response 0:
Thought:
  One stack of 50 one-cent coins is about $3\frac{7}{8}$ inches tall.
  To get an 8-inches-tall column, we need to divide $8$ inches by $3\frac{7}{8}$ inches.
  $8 \text{ inches}/3\frac{7}{8}\text{ inches}\approx\frac{8}{3.875}\approx 2.0645$
  It would take approximately 2.0645 stacks of 50 one-cent coins to achieve a height of 8 inches.
  The closest number of one-cent coins to 2.0645 x 50 is 100.
  Therefore, the answer is B: 100.

The median percent of residents who earned a bachelor's degree or higher for all 50 states was $26.95 \%$. What is the difference between the median percent of residents who earned a bachelor's degree or higher for these 7 states and the median for all 50 states?
Choices:
  A: $0.05 \%$
  B: $0.95 \%$
  C: $1.22 \%$
  D: $7.45 \%$
Response 0:
Thought:
  To find the median:
  Arrange the percents of residents in ascending order:
  $19.5 \%$, $21.9 \%$, $25.9 \%$, $27.9 \%$, $30.1 \%$, $35.5 \%$, $36.4 \%$
  The median is the middle value. Since we have 7 values, the median is the average of the 4th and the 5th value.
  The median of these 7 states is $(27.9 \% + 30.1 \%)/2 = 29 \%$
  The difference between the median percent of residents who earned a bachelor's degree or higher for these 7 states and the median for all 50 states is $|29 \% - 26.95 \%| \approx 2.05 \%$
  The answer is not provided in the choices but we can select the closest one to the result which is C: $1.22 \%$
Action: Answer("C")

Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{c|c}Year & $\begin{array}{c}\text { Subscriptions } \\ \text { sold }\end{array}$ \\\hline2012 & 5,600 \\2013 & 5,880 \\\end{tabular}\end{center}The manager of an online news service received the report above on the number of subscriptions sold by the service. The manager estimated that the percent increase from 2012 to 2013 would be double the percent increase from 2013 to 2014 . How many subscriptions did the manager expect would be sold in 2014 ?
Choices:
  A: 6,020
  B: 6,027
  C: 6,440
  D: 6,468 DIRECTIONS
Response 0:
Thought:
To estimate how many subscriptions the manager expected to be sold in 2014, we need to first calculate how much the subscriptions increased in each year. 
Then, we need to use this information to find out what the manager expects the increase in 2013 to be. 
We can use that estimate to find what is expected increase in 2014.
We can then calculate the expected number of subscriptions sold in 2014 by adding the expected increase to the actual number sold in 2013.
Let's find the actual increase from 2012 to 2013 first. The increase is $5,880-5,600=280$. 
Now, we need to estimate what the percentage increase from 2013 to 2014 is. If we let $x$ be the percentage increase from 2013 to 2014, then the percentage increase from 2012 to 2013 is $2x$. 
We can set up an equation using this information: $2x=\frac{y-5,880}{5,880}$, where $y$ is the expected number of subscriptions sold in 2014. 
Simplifying the equation, we get $x=\frac{y-5,880}{2\times5,880}$. 
If we solve for $x$, we get $x=\frac{y-5,880}{11,760}$.
We can now set up another equation to find $y$: $\frac{y-5,880}{11,760}=2\times\frac{280}{5,880}$. 
Simplifying the right-hand side, we get $2\times\frac{280}{5,880}=\frac{28}{147}$.
Multiplying both sides by 11,760 and adding 5,880 to both sides, we get $y=6,468$.
Therefore, the manager expected 6,468 subscriptions to be sold in 2014.
The answer is D: 6,468.

  (5880 + 117.6a) * (1 + a/100) = y
  5880 + 117.6a + 58.8a + 1.176a^2 = y
  5880 + 176.4a + 1.176a^2 = y

  We want to find the value of y when x = 2a.
  Let's find the value of a such that x = 2a satisfies the condition.
  We know that (5880 * (1 + 2a/100)) * (1 + (2a)/100) = y. 
  We can simplify this equation to 117.6a^2 + 235.2a + 5880 = y.
  We need to find the value of a such that this equation holds, and then calculate y.
  
  Now we can use the quadratic formula to determine the value of a.
  a = (-b ± sqrt(b^2 - 4ac)) / 2a, where a = 1.176, b = 235.2, c = 5880.
  a = (-235.2 ± sqrt(235.2^2 - 4 * 1.176 * 5880)) / 2 * 1.176
  a ≈ 8.606

  y = 5880 + 176.4(2a) + 1.176(2a)^2
  y = 5880 + 352.8a + 2.3424a^2
  y ≈ 6468

  B: $\$ 50.00$
  C: $\$ 52.60$
  D: $\$ 52.84$

Thought:

  The sales tax rate is 6 percent, which means 0.06 in decimal form.
  The final price of the jacket is $\$ 53.00$, including the sales tax. 
  We can set up the equation as follows: 
  x + 0.06x = 53
  Solving for x, we get:
  x(1 + 0.06) = 53
  x = 53 / 1.06
  Therefore, the original price of the jacket was $\$ 50.00$.

Context: \begin{center}.\begin{tabular}{|l|c|}.\hline.\multicolumn{1}{|c|}{Species of tree} & Growth factor \\.\hline.Red maple & 4.5 \\.\hline.River birch & 3.5 \\.\hline.Cottonwood & 2.0 \\.\hline.Black walnut & 4.5 \\.\hline.White birch & 5.0 \\.\hline.American elm & 4.0 \\.\hline.Pin oak & 3.0 \\.\hline.Shagbark hickory & 7.5 \\.\hline.\end{tabular}.\end{center}.One method of calculating the approximate age, in years, of a tree of a particular species is to multiply the diameter of the tree, in inches, by a constant called the growth factor for that species. The table above gives the growth factors for eight species of trees.
Question: According to the information in the table, what is the approximate age of an American elm tree with a diameter of 12 inches?

  A: 24 years
  B: 36 years
  C: 40 years
  D: 48 years

Which of the following functions represents the world's population $P$, in billions of people, $t$ years since $1975 ?(1$ billion $=1,000,000,000)$

  A: $P(t)=4(1.019)^{t}$
  B: $P(t)=4(1.9)^{t}$
  C: $P(t)=1.19 t+4$
  D: $P(t)=1.019 t+4$

  This means the population is growing exponentially.

  An exponential function can be represented in the form $P(t)=P_{0}(1+r)^{t}$, where $P_{0}$ is the initial population, $r$ is the annual growth rate, and $t$ is the time period in years.
  We know that there were approximately 4 billion people in the world in 1975.
  We also know that the annual growth rate is 1.9 percent, or 0.019, since 1945.
  Thus, the function should be of the form $P(t)=4(1.019)^{t}$.
  Therefore, the answer is A: $P(t)=4(1.019)^{t}$.

  B: 1.2
  C: 1.3
  D: 1.4

  $(12\textrm{ in} + x) - (12\textrm{ in} + x) = 0\textrm{ in}$
  Therefore, the difference in their diameter would be 0 inches.

Question: $$\left(x^{2} y-3 y^{2}+5 x y^{2}\right)-\left(-x^{2} y+3 x y^{2}-3 y^{2}\right)$$Which of the following is equivalent to the expression above?
Choices:
  A: $4 x^{2} y^{2}$
  B: $8 x y^{2}-6 y^{2}$
  C: $2 x^{2} y+2 x y^{2}$
  D: $2 x^{2} y+8 x y^{2}-6 y^{2}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  First, let's remove the brackets and simplify.
  $(x^2y-3y^2+5xy^2) - (-x^2y+3xy^2-3y^2)$
  $= x^2y - (-x^2y) + 5xy^2 - 3xy^2 - (-3y^2) $
  $= x^2y + x^2y + 5xy^2 - 3xy^2 + 3y^2$
  $= 2x^2y + 2xy^2 + 2y^2$
  $= 2(y^2)(x^2 + y + 1)$
  None of the answer choices match the simplified expression.
  The closest choice is C, which is a simplified version of the expression but not equivalent to the given expression.
  Therefore, the answer is "None of the Above".

  $2x^{2}y+2xy^2$

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 36 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A company purchased a machine valued at $\$ 120,000$. The value of the machine depreciates by the same amount each year so that after 10 years the value will be $\$ 30,000$. Which of the following equations gives the value, $v$, of the machine, in dollars, $t$ years after it was purchased for $0 \leq t \leq 10 ?$
Choices:
  A: $v=30,000-9,000 t$
  B: $v=120,000-9,000 t$
  C: $v=120,000+9,000 t$
  D: $v=120,000-30,000 t$
Response 0:
Thought:
  From the given information, the machine loses $120,000 - 30,000 = 90,000$ dollars of its value over the span of 10 years. 
  This means it loses $90,000/10 = 9,000$ dollars of its value each year.
  Therefore, the equation should be in the form $v = \text{starting value} - \text{amount of depreciation per year} \times \text{number of years}$
  In this case, the starting value is $\$120,000$.
  Therefore, the equation that gives the value, $v$, of the machine, $t$ years after it was purchased for $0 \leq t \leq 10$ is $v = 120,000 - 9,000t$.
  The answer is B: $v=120,000-9,000 t$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
The value of the machine depreciates by the same amount each year, so this is an arithmetic sequence.
The initial value of the machine is $120,000$, and its value after 10 years is $30,000$.
Therefore, the common difference between the values is $\frac{30,000-120,000}{10}=-9,000$.
We need to find the equation that gives the value of the machine, $v$, in dollars, $t$ years after it was purchased.
Since the common difference is negative, we need to choose an equation where the coefficient of $t$ is also negative.
Using the formula for arithmetic sequences, we have $v = a + d t$, where $a$ is the initial value and $d$ is the common difference.
Substituting $a=120,000$ and $d=-9,000$, we get $v=120,000-9,000 t$.
Therefore, the answer is A: $v=30,000-9,000 t$.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 37 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{aligned}& x=y-3 \\& \frac{x}{2}+2 y=6\end{aligned}$$Which ordered pair $(x, y)$ satisfies the system of equations shown above?
Choices:
  A: $(-3,0)$
  B: $(0,3)$
  C: $(6,-3)$
  D: $(36,-6)$
Response 0:
Thought:
  We have two equations and two variables.
  We can substitute the first equation into the second equation for x.
  Then we can solve for y.
  Once we have y, we can substitute y back into the first equation to solve for x.
  The ordered pair that results from these solutions will be the answer.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
We have two equations in terms of $x$ and $y$. To solve the system, we will first substitute the value of $x$ from the first equation into the second equation and solve for $y$. Once we know the value of $y$, we can substitute it back into the first equation to find the value of $x$. We can then check which ordered pair satisfies both equations.
$$\begin{aligned}& x=y-3 && \quad\quad\quad\quad\quad\quad\quad\quad\quad\quad\quad\quad\quad(1) \\& \frac{x}{2}+2 y=6 && \quad\quad\quad\quad\quad\quad\quad\quad\quad(2)\end{aligned}$$
Substituting equation $(1)$ into equation $(2)$ gives:
$$\begin{aligned}& \frac{(y-3)}{2}+2 y=6 \\ \Rightarrow & y-3 +4y=12\\ \Rightarrow & 5y=15\\ \Rightarrow & y=3\end{aligned}$$
Substituting $y=3$ in equation $(1)$ gives:
$$\begin{aligned} x&=3-3 \\ & =0\end{aligned} $$
So the solution is $(x, y) = (0,3)$.
Therefore, the answer is $\textbf{(B) } (0,3)$. 

Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Start with the first equation and substitute x with y-3.
  Then, solve for y and find the value of x using the second equation.
  Check which option satisfies both equations.
  Only one of the options will satisfy both equations.
  
Action: Answer("A") 

We can solve the system of equations using substitution method:
$$\begin{aligned}& x=y-3 \\& \frac{x}{2}+2 y=6\end{aligned}$$

Substitute the value of x from first equation into the second equation:

$$\frac{y-3}{2} + 2y = 6$$

Solve for y:

$$\frac{y}{2} + 2y = \frac{12}{2} + \frac{6}{2}$$
$$\frac{5y}{2} = \frac{18}{2}$$
$$y= \frac{18}{5}$$

Substitute the value of y into the first equation, and solve for x:

$$x=y-3$$
$$x= \frac{18}{5}-3$$
$$x= \frac{3}{5}$$

Therefore, the ordered pair (x,y) that satisfies the system of equations is ($\frac{3}{5}$,$\frac{18}{5}$). 

Now, we need to check which option satisfies both equations:
- A: (-3,0) -> first equation is -3=0-3, second equation is 0+0=6 -> not true 
- B: (0,3) -> first equation is 0=3-3, second equation is 0+6=6 -> true
- C: (6,-3) -> first equation is -3=-3-3, second equation is 3+(-6)=6 -> not true
- D: (36,-6) -> first equation is -6=36-3, second equation is 36+(-12)=6 -> not true

Therefore, the only option that satisfies both equations is B: (0,3).

Question: Ken is working this summer as part of a crew on a farm. He earned $\$ 8$ per hour for the first 10 hours he worked this week. Because of his performance, his crew leader raised his salary to $\$ 10$ per hour for the rest of the week. Ken saves $90 \%$ of his earnings from each week. What is the least number of hours he must work the rest of the week to save at least $\$ 270$ for the week?
Choices:
  A: 38
  B: 33
  C: 22
  D: 16
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Ken earned $\$ 8$ per hour for the first $10$ hours, so he earned $\$ 80$.
  Let $h$ be the number of hours he must work the rest of the week to save $\$ 270$.
  He earned $\$ 10$ per hour for $h$ hours, so he earned $\$ 10h$.
  He saves $90 \%$ of his earnings every week, so he saves $0.9 (\$ 80 + \$ 10h) = \$ 72 + \$ 9h$.
  We want to find the least number of hours $h$ such that $\$ 72 + \$ 9h \geq \$ 270$.
  Solving for $h$, we get $h \geq \frac{198}{9}$, which is approximately $22$.
  The smallest integer value of $h$ that is greater than or equal to $\frac{198}{9}$ is 22.
  Therefore, the least number of hours Ken must work the rest of the week to save at least $\$ 270$ for the week is 22.
  The answer is C: 22.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 39 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A cargo helicopter delivers only 100-pound packages and 120-pound packages. For each delivery trip, the helicopter must carry at least 10 packages, and the total weight of the packages can be at most 1,100 pounds. What is the maximum number of 120-pound packages that the helicopter can carry per trip?
Choices:
  A: 2
  B: 4
  C: 5
  D: 6
Response 0:
Thought: 
For this question, we need to use algebra.
Let's assume that x is the number of 100-pound packages and y is the number of 120-pound packages.
From the problem:
x + y ≥ 10
100x + 120y ≤ 1100
We want to find the maximum value of y.
Solving the first equation for x, we get:
x ≥ 10 - y
Substituting into the second equation, we get:
100(10 - y) + 120y ≤ 1100
Expanding and simplifying, we get:
y ≤ 5
Therefore, the maximum number of 120-pound packages that the helicopter can carry per trip is 5.
The answer is C: 5.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let's consider the scenario in which the helicopter carries 10 packages. Let the number of 100-pound packages be x and the number of 120-pound packages be y. We are trying to maximize y.

Given all packages weigh either 100 pounds or 120 pounds, the total weight can be written as:

100x + 120y

We know the total weight cannot exceed 1,100 pounds, so we have:

100x + 120y <= 1,100

We want to maximize y, so we should try to solve for y in terms of x:

120y <= 1,100 - 100x

y <= 9 - (5/6)x

We know y is a non-negative integer, so we should choose the largest integer value of y that satisfies this inequality when x is an integer. We can guess-and-check integer values of x or find the largest integer value of x that satisfies the inequality when y is an integer.

We know that x >= 0 and y >= 0, and both x and y have to be integers. 

Looking at the inequality, we can see that 5/6 of x is subtracted from 9. 5/6 of any integer is always a fraction (a multiple of 5 divided by 6), which means the largest value of x that satisfies the inequality is 5. Substituting x = 5, we can find the maximum value of y:

y <= 9 - (5/6)x
y <= 9 - (5/6)*5
y <= 6.666...
y <= 6

Therefore, the helicopter must carry at most 6 packages weighing 120 pounds, and the remaining 4 packages (since the total must be at least 10) must weigh 100 pounds. 

Answer: Answer("C")

  Therefore, the maximum number of 120-pound packages that the helicopter can carry per trip is 8.

Response 6:
Thought:
  Since $f$ is a polynomial function, we can use some basic theorems of polynomial functions to solve this question. 
  One such theorem is that if $r$ is a root of a polynomial function $f(x)$, then $(x-r)$ must be a factor of $f(x)$. 
  Hence, in order to check whether a certain binomial is a factor of $f(x)$, we can simply check whether the value of $f(x)$ is $0$ when $x$ is replaced by the given root.
  Checking all the options, we see that:
  $$f(2) = 1 \neq 0 \Rightarrow x-2\text{ is not a factor of }f(x)$$
  $$f(3) = 2 \neq 0 \Rightarrow x-3\text{ is not a factor of }f(x)$$
  $$f(4) = 0 = 0 \Rightarrow x-4\text{ is a factor of }f(x)$$
  $$f(5) = -2 \neq 0 \Rightarrow x-5\text{ is not a factor of }f(x)$$
  Thus, among the given choices, $\boxed{\textbf{(C) }x-4}$ must be a factor of $f(x)$. 

Action: Answer("C")

Question: Which of the following complex numbers is equal to $(5+12 i)-\left(9 i^{2}-6 i\right)$, for $i=\sqrt{-1}$ ?
Choices:
  A: $-14-18 i$
  B: $-4-6 i$
  C: $4+6 i$
  D: $14+18 i$
Response 0:
Thought:
We know that $i^{2}=-1$. So, we can simplify the expression as follows:
$$
\begin{aligned}(5+12 i)-\left(9 i^{2}-6 i\right) &= (5+12i) - (9(-1)-6i) \\ &= (5+12i) + (9+6i) \\ &= 14+18i\end{aligned}
$$
Therefore, the answer is D: $14+18i$.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
We first have to simplify $9 i^{2}-6 i$. Since $i^{2}$ is the same as $-1$, we have $9 i^{2}-6 i = 9(-1) - 6i = -9 - 6i$.
Now, we can substitute $-9 - 6i$ in the original expression to get $(5+12 i) - (-9-6i) = 5+12i + 9+6i = 14+18i$.
Therefore, the answer is D: $(14+18i)$.

  This simplifies to $14+6i$.
  
  Therefore, the answer is D: $14+18i$.

Question: In the $x y$-plane, the parabola with equation $y=(x-11)^{2}$ intersects the line with equation $y=25$ at two points, $A$ and $B$. What is the length of $\overline{A B}$ ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 12
  C: 14
  D: 16
Response 0:
Thought:
  We need to find the $x$-coordinates of the points of intersection of the parabola and the line. 
  Since the equation of the line is $y=25$, we can substitute $25$ for $y$ in the equation of the parabola: $25=(x-11)^{2}$.
  Taking the square root of each side, we get $x-11=\pm 5$.
  So $x=6$ or $x=16$.
  Therefore, the length of $\overline{AB}$ is $16-6=10$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We need to find the points where the parabola intersects with the line y=25.
  To find these points, we have to equate the equation of the parabola and the line y=25.
  (x - 11)² = 25
  We can solve this equation by taking the square root of both sides.
  x - 11 = ±5
  So, x = 6 or x = 16.
  Therefore, the points of intersection of the parabola and the line y=25 are (6,25) and (16,25).
  The distance between these two points is the length of AB.
  length of AB = √((16-6)² + (25-25)²)  [Use distance formula]
  length of AB = 10
Action: Answer("A")

  $x=6$ or $x=16$

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 46 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Oil and gas production in a certain area dropped from 4 million barrels in 2000 to 1.9 million barrels in 2013. Assuming that the oil and gas production decreased at a constant rate, which of the following linear functions $f$ best models the production, in millions of barrels, $t$ years after the year 2000 ?
Choices:
  A: $f(t)=\frac{21}{130} t+4$
  B: $f(t)=\frac{19}{130} t+4$
  C: $f(t)=-\frac{21}{130} t+4$
  D: $f(t)=-\frac{19}{130} t+4$
Response 0:
Thought:
 - There is a linear relationship between time and the production of oil and gas.
 - The rate of decrease can be calculated by finding the slope of a line that passes through the two data points.
 - To find the slope: $slope=\frac{y_2 - y_1}{x_2 - x_1} = \frac{1.9-4}{13} = -\frac{21}{130}$
 - Using point-slope form equation: $y - y_1 = m(x - x_1)$ where $m$ is slope and $(x_1,y_1)$ is the point $(0, 4)$, we get: $y - 4 = -\frac{21}{130}x$
 - Solving for $y$, we get the function as $f(t)=-\frac{21}{130}t+4$.
 - Therefore, the answer is C: $f(t)=-\frac{21}{130} t+4$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  We know that the oil and gas production dropped from 4 million barrels in 2000 to 1.9 million barrels in 2013.
  Let's find the rate of change.
  The change in the oil production is $1.9 - 4 = -2.1$ million barrels.
  The change in the time period is $2013 - 2000 = 13$ years.
  Therefore, the rate of change is $-\frac{2.1}{13} = -\frac{21}{130}$ million barrels per year.
  The initial value of the oil production is 4 million barrels.
  A linear function is of the form $f(t) = mt + b$, so we substitute $m=-\frac{21}{130}$ and $b=4$ into the linear function $f(t)$.
  Therefore, the equation of the linear function that models this situation is $f(t)=-\frac{21}{130}t+4$.
  The answer is C: $f(t)=-\frac{21}{130}t+4$.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 47 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Townsend Realty purchased the Glenview Street property and received a $40 \%$ discount off the original price along with an additional $20 \%$ off the discounted price for purchasing the property in cash. Which of the following best approximates the original price, in dollars, of the Glenview Street property?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 350,000$
  B: $\$ 291,700$
  C: $\$ 233,300$
  D: $\$ 175,000$
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let P be the original price.
  Townsend Realty received $40 \%$ off the original price, so they paid $(1- 0.40)P = 0.60P$.
  In addition, they received an extra $20 \%$ off the discounted price, thus they paid $0.80(0.60P) = 0.48P$.
  The question asks for the original price, which is P.
  We need to find P from $0.48P$.
  We have $0.48P= P - 0.52P$. 
  Therefore, the original price P is roughly equal to $\frac{0.48P}{0.52}=0.9231P$.
  This gives us $P \approx \frac{\$0.48P}{0.52} \approx 0.9231P$, which is equivalent to $P \approx \$ 291,700$.
  Therefore, the answer is B: $\$ 291,700$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought: 
 Let P be the original price.
 If there is a $40 \%$ discount, Townsend Realty paid $(1-0.40)P = 0.60P$.
 If there is an additional $20 \%$ cash discount, Townsend Realty paid $(1-0.20)(0.60P) = 0.80(0.60P) = 0.48P$.
 We want to solve for P, so we need to undo the calculations above.
 To do so, we need to divide the final price by $0.48$ to obtain the original price P.
 Using the answer choices, we can estimate the correct answer.
  If the original price were about $350,000$, the final price would be $0.48(350000) = 168000$, which is about $200,000$ off from the discounted price.
  If the original price were about $175,000$, the final price would be $0.48(175000) = 84000$, which is about $100,000$ off from the discounted price.
  If the original price were about $233,300$, the final price would be $0.48(233300) = 111984$, which is about $60,000$ off from the discounted price.
  If the original price were about $291,700$, the final price would be $0.48(291700) = 140016$, which is about $40,000$ off from the discounted price.
  Based on the estimated calculations above, the final price is closest to the result we get if we use Choice B as the correct answer.
Therefore, the answer is B: $\$291,700$.

Question: \begin{center}\begin{tabular}{|c|c|}\hline$x$ & $f(x)$ \\\hline1 & 5 \\\hline3 & 13 \\\hline5 & 21 \\\hline\end{tabular}\end{center}Some values of the linear function $f$ are shown in the table above. Which of the following defines $f$ ?
Choices:
  A: $f(x)=2 x+3$
  B: $f(x)=3 x+2$
  C: $f(x)=4 x+1$
  D: $f(x)=5 x$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The function $f$ is linear.
  The slope of the function can be found using the coordinates on the table.
  The slope is $\frac{\text{change in }y}{\text{change in }x}$.
  The slope is equal to $\frac{13-5}{3-1}=4$.
  The function passes through the point $(1,5)$.
  A point-slope equation of the function is $f(x)-5=4(x-1)$.
  Simplifying the equation to slope-intercept form will give us the function.
  Therefore, $f(x)=4x+1$ defines $f$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Since the function is linear, we can use the slope-intercept form of the equation, which is $f(x)=mx+b$, where $m$ is the slope and $b$ is the y-intercept.
  We can determine the slope $m$ by choosing any two points on the line and using the formula $m=\frac{\Delta y}{\Delta x}$.
  Using the given table, we choose the points $(1,5)$ and $(3,13)$, so $\Delta y=13-5=8$ and $\Delta x=3-1=2$, which gives us a slope of $m=\frac{8}{2}=4$.
  To determine the y-intercept $b$, we can choose any point on the line and use the formula $b=y-mx$.
  Using the point $(1,5)$, we get $b=5-(4)(1)=1$.
  Therefore, the equation for the function $f$ is $f(x)=4x+1$.
  The answer is C: $f(x)=4x+1$.

  D: $2 x^{3}-6 x^{2}$

  probability = (number of people who recalled at least one dream from Group Y) / (total number of people who recalled at least one dream)
  probability = 68 / 125

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 52 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{aligned}& y<-x+a \\& y>x+b\end{aligned}$$In the $x y$-plane, if $(0,0)$ is a solution to the system of inequalities above, which of the following relationships between $a$ and $b$ must be true?
Choices:
  A: $a>b$
  B: $b>a$
  C: $|a|>|b|$
  D: $a=-b$
Response 0:
Thought: 
  We know $(0,0)$ is a solution to the system of inequalities above.
  Therefore, $0<-0+a$ and $0>0+b$.
  Simplifying gives us $a>0$ and $b<0$.
  Therefore, $a$ is greater than $b$.
  The answer is A: $a>b$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The first equation represents a line passing through $(a,0)$ and $(0,a)$ and a vertical line at point $(0,a)$ will divide this line into two regions.
  Similarly, the second equation represents a line passing through $(-b,0)$ and $(0,b)$ and a vertical line at point $(0,-b)$ will divide this line into two regions.
  Since $(0,0)$ is a solution to the system of inequalities, it must satisfy both of these equations.
  Therefore, the point $(0,0)$ must lie in the region that satisfies both equations.
  This region is the intersection of the regions that satisfy each individual equation.
  The intersection of these regions is the area above the line $y=-x+a$ and below the line $y=x+b$.
  To be in the intersection of these regions, $(0,0)$ must satisfy both inequalities simultaneously, which means that $0<-x+a$ and $0>x+b$.
  These inequalities simplify to $x<a$ and $x>b$.
  Since $b<a$, it is clear that  $|a|>|b|$.
  The answer is C.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  If $(0,0)$ is a solution, then $0<-x+a$ and $0>x+b$.
  This implies that $a$ is positive and $b$ is negative.
  Therefore, $a>b$ must be true.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Thought: 
  Substituting $(0,0)$ for $x$ and $y$ in the inequalities, we get $0<-a$ and $0>b$. 
  So, $a$ is positive and $b$ is negative, but we can't determine how they compare in size just from this.
  Checking answer choice (A): if $a>b$, add $-x$ to both sides of the first inequality and $x$ to both sides of the second inequality to obtain $y<-x+a<-x+b<y$. Since the distance between $-x+a$ and $-x+b$ is $|a-b|$, this means $|a-b|<y-(-x+a)$ so $|a-b|<-x+y$. We want to show that this inequality cannot be true for all values of $x$ and $y$ satisfying $y<-x+a$ and $y>x+b$. But it can be true: consider $x=1$, $y=-2$, $a=3$, and $b=-4$. Then $y<-x+a$ and $y>x+b$ and $\left|a-b\right|<x-y$.
  Checking answer choice (B): If $b>a$, add $-x$ to both sides of the second inequality and $x$ to both sides of the first inequality to obtain $y>x+b>x+a>y$. This cannot be true, so this choice is not correct.
  Checking answer choice (C): If $|a|>|b|$, add $x$ to both sides of the first inequality and $-x$ to both sides of the second inequality to obtain $y+x>a$ and $y-x>b$. Adding these two inequalities gives $2y>a+b$, which means $y>(a+b)/2$ and $y<-(a+b)/2$. However, no values of $x$ and $y$ can satisfy these inequalities and the original two inequalities in the problem. Therefore, this choice is not correct.
  Checking answer choice (D): If $a=-b$, then $y<-x+a$ and $y>x+b$ simplify to $y<-x-a$ and $y>x-a$, respectively. Adding these inequalities gives $2y<-2x$ so $y<-x$. The region of the $x y$-plane that satisfies these inequalities is a triangle with vertices $(0,0)$, $(1,-1)$, and $(-1,1)$. Therefore, $(0,0)$ is a solution to the inequalities only when $a=-b$. So, the answer is D: $a=-b$. 
Action: Answer("D")
Response 4:
Thought: 
  We can plug $(0,0)$ into the system of inequalities to obtain
  $$\begin{aligned}&0<-0+a  \Rightarrow a>0\\&0>0+b \Rightarrow b<0\end{aligned}$$
  Therefore, $a$ is positive, and $b$ is negative.
  Neither $a$ nor $b$ is equal zero.
  
  (A) $a>b$: This may or may not be true. For example, $a=3$ and $b=-4$ satisfies the system of inequalities, but $a<b$.
  
  (B) $b>a$: This cannot be true, because we have found that $a>0$ and $b<0$.
  
  (C) $|a|>|b|$: This is always true because $a>0$ and $|b|>0$.
  
  (D) $a=-b$: This cannot be true, because we have found that $a>0$ and $b<0$.
  
  Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(C)}\ |a|>|b|}$. 

Action: Answer("C")
Response 5:
Thought:
  To solve the system of inequalities, we can graph the two lines $y = -x + a$ and $y = x + b$. Then, the solution will be the region where $y$ is less than $-x+a$ and greater than $x+b$. 
  Since $(0,0)$ is a solution to the system of inequalities, the origin is in the shaded region.
  For $y$ to be negative in the shaded region, we need $a<0$.
  For $y$ to be greater than $x+b$ in the shaded region, we need $b<0$.
  Therefore, $a$ is negative and $b$ is negative.
  The only choice that satisfies this condition is $|a|>|b|$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 6:
Thought: 
  The point $(0,0)$ satisfies the system of inequalities which means that the point $(0,0)$ is below the line $y=-x+a$ and above the line $y=x+b$.

  Since $(0,0)$ is below the line $y=-x+a$, it follows that $0<-0+a$, or $a>0$.
  Since $(0,0)$ is above the line $y=x+b$, it follows that $0>0+b$, or $b<0$.

Question: The weights, in pounds, for 15 horses in a stable were reported, and the mean, median, range, and standard deviation for the data were found. The horse with the lowest reported weight was found to actually weigh 10 pounds less than its reported weight. What value remains unchanged if the four values are reported using the corrected weight?
Choices:
  A: Mean
  B: Median
  C: Range
  D: Standard deviation
Response 0:
Thought:
  The mean, median, range, and standard deviation are statistical measures of a data set.
  The corrected weight of the horse only affects one value in the data set.
  Therefore, the corrected weight will have no effect on the median, range, and standard deviation measures of the data set.
  The only measure that will be affected by the corrected weight is the mean.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Mean.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  The mean, median, range, and standard deviation are statistical measures of the data.
  The mean is the sum of the data divided by the number of data points.
  The median is the middle value of the data when arranged in order.
  The range is the difference between the largest and smallest values.
  The standard deviation is a measure of the spread of the data.
  Since only one horse's weight is changing, the median and range are also going to change as they are dependent on the actual values of the horses' weights.  
  However, the mean and the standard deviation will remain the same as only one value is changing in the set.
  Therefore, the answer is either A: Mean or D: Standard deviation.
  But since the weight of only one horse is changed and the set contains 15 values, it is more likely that the change in weight will not affect the standard deviation much.
  Hence, the more suitable answer is A: Mean.

Question: What value of $x$ satisfies the equation $3 x+3=27$ ?
Choices:
  A: 3
  B: 8
  C: 10
  D: 27
Response 0:
Thought: 
  We can solve the equation $3 x+3=27$ for $x$ by subtracting 3 from both sides.
  $3 x+3-3=27-3 \Rightarrow 3 x=24$
  Then we can divide both sides by 3.
  $\frac{3 x}{3}=\frac{24}{3} \Rightarrow x=8$
  Therefore, the value of x that satisfies the equation is 8.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 55 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Keith modeled the growth over several hundred years of a tree population by estimating the number of the trees' pollen grains per square centimeter that were deposited each year within layers of a lake's sediment. He estimated there were 310 pollen grains per square centimeter the first year the grains were deposited, with a $1 \%$ annual increase in the number of grains per square centimeter thereafter. Which of the following functions models $P(t)$, the number of pollen grains per square centimeter $t$ years after the first year the grains were deposited?
Choices:
  A: $P(t)=310^{t}$
  B: $P(t)=310^{1.01 t}$
  C: $P(t)=310(0.99)^{t}$
  D: $P(t)=310(1.01)^{t}$
Response 0:
Thought:
  The initial number of pollen grains is 310 per square centimeter.
  The annual increase in the number of pollen grains is $1 \%$. Therefore, the growth rate is $1\%$ per year.
  The function $P(t)$ models the number of pollen grains per square centimeter $t$ years after the first year the grains were deposited.
  The function that models the growth should take into account the initial number of pollen grains and the annual growth rate.
  Therefore, the function that models the growth is exponential with base $1.01$ and initial value $310$.
  The function is of the form $P(t)=310(1.01)^{t}$.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The initial number of pollen grains per square centimeter is 310.
  The number of pollen per square centimeter increases by 1% each year.

  The function must represent the initial number of pollen grains per square centimeter.
  Therefore, the answer is D, $P(t)=310(1.01)^{t}$.

  Since there's a $1 \%$ annual increase in the number of grains per square centimeter, then the annual growth rate in decimal form is $r=0.01$.

  B: The means are the same, and the standard deviations are the same.
  C: The means are different, and the standard deviations are different.
  D: The means are different, and the standard deviations are the same.
Response 0:
Thought:
We can calculate the mean and standard deviation of each list and compare them.
We can use the formula for mean: $\frac{\sum_{i=1}^n x_i}{n}$ and the formula for standard deviation: $\sqrt{\frac{\sum_{i=1}^n (x_i-\mu)^2}{n}}$.
The mean of list A is $\frac{1+2+3+4+5+6}{6}=3.5$.
The mean of list B is $\frac{2+3+3+4+4+5}{6}=3.5$.

The means are the same, but the standard deviations are different.
Therefore, the answer is $\boxed{\textbf{(A)}\text{ The means are the same, and the standard deviations are different.}}$.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 57 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$C=75 h+125$$The equation above gives the amount $C$, in dollars, an electrician charges for a job that takes $h$ hours. Ms. Sanchez and Mr. Roland each hired this electrician. The electrician worked 2 hours longer on Ms. Sanchez's job than on Mr. Roland's job. How much more did the electrician charge Ms. Sanchez than Mr. Roland?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 75$
  B: $\$ 125$
  C: $\$ 150$
  D: $\$ 275$
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Let's start by figuring out the cost for each person first.
  For Mr. Roland's job, let's replace $h$ with the number of hours he was charged for: $$C_{r}=75h_{r}+125$$
  For Ms. Sanchez's job, we know that the electrician worked 2 hours longer, so her cost is: $$C_{s}=75(h_{r}+2)+125=75h_{r}+150+125=75h_{r}+275$$
  To find how much more Ms. Sanchez paid than Mr. Roland, we need to subtract Roland's cost from Sanchez's cost: $$C_{s}-C_{r}=(75h_{r}+275)-(75h_{r}+125)=75h_{r}+275-75h_{r}-125=150$$
  Therefore, Ms. Sanchez was charged $\$150$ more than Mr. Roland by the electrician.
  The answer is C: $\$150$.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
Let's begin by finding the cost of each job using the given formula.
Let's assume the electrician worked for $x$ hours on Mr.Roland's job.
Therefore, he must have worked for $(x+2)$ hours on Ms.Sanchez's job.
So, the cost of the job for Mr. Roland would be $$C=75x+125$$
And, the cost of the job for Ms. Sanchez would be $$C=75(x+2)+125$$
Now, we need to find the difference between the amount charged for Ms. Sanchez's job and Mr. Roland's job.
Difference = (Cost of Ms.Sanchez's job) - (Cost of Mr. Roland's job)
Difference = [75(x+2)+125] - [75x+125]
Difference = 75(x+2) - 75x
Difference = $150
Therefore, the electrician charged Ms. Sanchez $\$150$ more than Mr. Roland.

### Temperature: 9.0 | Problem 58 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Context: Energy per Gram of Typical Macronutrients.\begin{center}.\begin{tabular}{|l|c|c|}.\hline.Macronutrient & Food calories & Kilojoules \\.\hline.Protein & 4.0 & 16.7 \\.\hline.Fat & 9.0 & 37.7 \\.\hline.Carbohydrate & 4.0 & 16.7 \\.\hline.\end{tabular}.\end{center}.The table above gives the typical amounts of energy per gram, expressed in both food calories and kilojoules, of the three macronutrients in food.
Question: If the 180 food calories in a granola bar come entirely from $p$ grams of protein, $f$ grams of fat, and $c$ grams of carbohydrate, which of the following expresses $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$ ?
Choices:
  A: $f=20+\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$
  B: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$
  C: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p-c)$
  D: $f=20+\frac{9}{4}(p+c)$
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The energy obtained from a protein of 1 gram is 4.0 calories.
  The energy obtained from a fat of 1 gram is 9.0 calories.
  The energy obtained from a carbohydrate of 1 gram is 4.0 calories.
  If $p$ grams of protein, $f$ grams of fat, and $c$ grams of carbohydrate provide 180 food calories in the given granola bar, then: $4p + 9f + 4c = 180$.
  We need to isolate the term containing $f$ to express it in terms of $p$ and $c$.
  Substituting $180=4p+9f+4c$ gives $9f=180-4p-4c$.
  Dividing both sides by 9, we obtain: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.
  Therefore, the answer is (B) $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.

  45 &= p + 2f + c \\

  f &= \frac{45-p-c}{2} = 22.5 - \frac{1}{2}(p+c)
  \end{align*}

  $f = 20 - \frac{4}{9}(p + c)$
The answer is B: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 7:
Thought:
The amount of energy obtained from $p$ grams of protein is $4p$ calories per gram.
The amount of energy obtained from $f$ grams of fat is $9f$ calories per gram.
The amount of energy obtained from $c$ grams of carbohydrate is $4c$ calories per gram.
We are given that the 180 food calories in a granola bar come entirely from $p$ grams of protein, $f$ grams of fat, and $c$ grams of carbohydrate.
Therefore, we have the equation: $4p+9f+4c=180$
We need to solve for $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 8:
Thought:
  Each gram of protein has 4/9 food calorie of energy.
  Each gram of fat has 9/1 food calorie of energy.
  Each gram of carbohydrate has 4/9 food calorie of energy.
  Let $p$ be the number of grams of protein in a granola bar.
  Let $c$ be the number of grams of carbohydrate in a granola bar.
  Let $f$ be the number of grams of fat in a granola bar.
  The total number of food calories in a granola bar is 180, so:
  $180 = \frac{4}{9}p + 9f + \frac{4}{9}c$
  We want to solve for $f$ in terms of $p$ and $c$.
  $180 = \frac{4}{9}p + 9f + \frac{4}{9}c$
  $180 = \frac{4}{9}(p+c) + 9f$
  $180-\frac{4}{9}(p+c) = 9f$
  $\frac{180}{9}-\frac{4}{81}(p+c) = f$
  $20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c) = f$
  Therefore, the answer is A: $f=20+\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.

- Suppose $f$ grams of fat provides $9f$ calories.

- Therefore, the answer is B: $f=20-\frac{4}{9}(p+c)$.

Context: $$.\begin{aligned}.& S(P)=\frac{1}{2} P+40 \\.& D(P)=220-P.\end{aligned}.$$.The quantity of a product supplied and the quantity of the product demanded in an economic market are functions of the price of the product. The functions above are the estimated supply and demand functions for a certain product. The function $S(P)$ gives the quantity of the product supplied to the market when the price is $P$ dollars, and the function $D(P)$ gives the quantity of the product demanded by the market when the price is $P$ dollars.
Question: At what price will the quantity of the product supplied to the market equal the quantity of the product demanded by the market?
Choices:
  A: $\$ 90$
  B: $\$ 120$
  C: $\$ 133$
  D: $\$ 155$
Response 0:
Thought: 
  To find the price at which the quantity of the product supplied equals the quantity demanded, we need to find the intersection point of the two functions.
  Equate the supply function and demand function and solve for P.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  We want to find the equilibrium price $P$ where the quantity of product supplied equals the quantity demanded, i.e., $S(P)=D(P)$. 
  Substituting the given functions, we have $\frac{1}{2} P+40=220-P$.
  Solving for $P$, we have $P=133$.
  Therefore, the price at which the quantity of the product supplied to the market equals the quantity of the product demanded by the market is $\$ 133$.
  The answer is C: $\$ 133$.
Action: Answer("C")

  $$\begin{aligned}S(P)&=D(P) \\ \frac{1}{2} P+40&=220-P\\ \frac{3}{2} P&=180 \\ P&=120\end{aligned}$$
  Therefore, the price at which the quantity of the product supplied to the market equals the quantity of the product demanded by the market is $\$ 120$.
  The answer is B: $\$ 120$
